	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">England national rugby league team</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/England_national_rugby_union_team" title="England national rugby union team">England national rugby union team</a> or <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_national_rugby_league_team" title="Great Britain national rugby league team">Great Britain national rugby league team</a>.</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the men's team. For the women's team, see <a href="/wiki/England_women%27s_national_rugby_league_team" title="England women&#39;s national rugby league team">England women's national rugby league team</a>.</div>

<a href="/wiki/1975_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="1975 Rugby League World Cup">1975</a>, <a href="/wiki/1995_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="1995 Rugby League World Cup">1995</a>, <a href="/wiki/2017_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2017 Rugby League World Cup">2017</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>England national rugby league team</b> represents England in international <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a>.
</p><p>The team, largely formed from the <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_national_rugby_league_team" title="Great Britain national rugby league team">Great Britain</a> team which also represented <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_rugby_league_team" title="Wales national rugby league team">Wales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_rugby_league_team" title="Scotland national rugby league team">Scotland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ireland_national_rugby_league_team" title="Ireland national rugby league team">Ireland</a>, is run under the auspices of the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_League" title="Rugby Football League">Rugby Football League</a>. It participates in the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="Rugby League World Cup">Rugby League World Cup</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_Four_Nations" title="Rugby League Four Nations">Four Nations</a> and Test matches.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The team dates to 1904, when they played against a mixture of Welsh and Scottish players in <a href="/wiki/Wigan" title="Wigan">Wigan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Until the 1950s, they regularly toured Australia and New Zealand and played both home and away matches against neighbours Wales and France, but when it was decided that Great Britain would tour the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a> instead of England, France and Wales became the only regular opponents.
</p><p>Their first appearance in the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="Rugby League World Cup">Rugby League World Cup</a> was in 1975, and they finished runners-up in <a href="/wiki/1975_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="1975 Rugby League World Cup">1975</a>, <a href="/wiki/1995_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="1995 Rugby League World Cup">1995</a> and <a href="/wiki/2017_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2017 Rugby League World Cup">2017</a>. England also competed in the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_European_Nations_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Rugby League European Nations Cup">European Nations Cup</a> and in 2006, an <a href="/wiki/England_Knights" title="England Knights">England 'A'</a> team competed for the <a href="/wiki/Federation_Shield" title="Federation Shield">Federation Shield</a>.
</p><p>England's main rivals historically were <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_rugby_league_team" title="Wales national rugby league team">Wales</a> and <a href="/wiki/France_national_rugby_league_team" title="France national rugby league team">France</a>, with the rivalries stretching back to 1908 and 1934 respectively. England's main rivals now are <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_rugby_league_team" title="Australia national rugby league team">Australia</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_national_rugby_league_team" title="New Zealand national rugby league team">New Zealand</a>.
</p><p>Traditionally a predominantly white kit is worn including white shorts and socks. However the jersey usually features some form of red, like red stripes, crosses or chevrons. These colours are similar to other English sporting teams and are the colours used on the national flag. In 2008, a new kit was introduced featuring a red cross on the front and red strips down the sides of the jersey, shorts and socks were white too with red strips.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Also in 2008, the Rugby Football League chose to abandon the traditional English lion on the badge in favour of a much simpler shield and <a href="/wiki/St_George_cross" class="mw-redirect" title="St George cross">cross</a> design.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Currently the team is ranked second in the world, behind <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_rugby_league_team" title="Australia national rugby league team">Australia</a>. <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Bennett_(rugby_league)" title="Wayne Bennett (rugby league)">Wayne Bennett</a> is the head coach, and <a href="/wiki/Sean_O%27Loughlin" title="Sean O&#39;Loughlin">Sean O'Loughlin</a> the captain.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=England_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_first_matches">The first matches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=England_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: The first matches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1895, twenty-one clubs split with the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_Union" title="Rugby Football Union">Rugby Football Union</a>, citing that they wanted to play professionally, and formed the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_League" title="Rugby Football League">Northern Rugby Football Union</a>. The twenty-one clubs were all from <a href="/wiki/Northern_England" title="Northern England">Northern England</a> and the players were largely working class. However it was not just English players who made the switch, Scottish and Welsh players also switched allegiance to the new code, wanting payments for playing. Switching heightened in the early 20th century with more Scottish and Welsh players leaving the RFU than ever before.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/England_national_rugby_union_team" title="England national rugby union team">England national rugby union team</a> had been playing international matches since 1871, but it was not until 1904, nine years after the formation of the new code, that an international rugby league match was played. At the start of 1903 season the Northern Union thought about international matches and scheduled a match for England on New Year's Day 1904 in <a href="/wiki/Oldham" title="Oldham">Oldham</a>. On that day though, the ground was frosty and the match was cancelled and it was rescheduled for April.
</p><p>On 5 April 1904 England competed against a team called "<a href="/wiki/Other_Nationalities_rugby_league_team" title="Other Nationalities rugby league team">Other Nationalities</a>", who were made up of ten Welshman and two Scotsman, including <a href="/wiki/George_Frater" title="George Frater">George Frater</a>, who captained the side. It was a period of experimentation for the Northern Union and each team had twelve players, not thirteen. At <a href="/wiki/Central_Park_(Wigan)" title="Central Park (Wigan)">Central Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wigan" title="Wigan">Wigan</a> the ground was muddy and in poor condition, however the match went ahead. England steamed into a 3–0 lead, from a try by <a href="/wiki/Warrington_Wolves" title="Warrington Wolves">Warrington's</a> <a href="/wiki/Jack_Fish_(rugby_league)" title="Jack Fish (rugby league)">Jackie Fish</a>. This is despite <a href="/wiki/Salford_Red_Devils" title="Salford Red Devils">Salford's</a> <a href="/wiki/James_Lomas_(rugby_league)" title="James Lomas (rugby league)">James Lomas</a> arriving late and causing England to start the match with eleven players. Fish missed the conversion and so the Other Nationalities were able to level the scores a little later, Welshman Thomas crashing over for a try. The conversion was missed and going into half-time the score was tied 3–3. In the second half Thomas went over for another try before <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Warriors" title="Wigan Warriors">Wigan's</a> Harris sealed a 9–3 win for the Other Nationalities in the final minutes of the match. A total of 6,000 spectators turned up for the match, which was considered a poor showing despite a <a href="/wiki/Broughton_Rangers" title="Broughton Rangers">Broughton Rangers</a> v Bradford cup clash being scheduled on the same day.
</p><p>In 1905 a match between the two sides was played at Bradford. This time England won 26–11 even though they were losing 11–0 at half-time. Wigan's <a href="/wiki/Jim_Leytham" title="Jim Leytham">Jim Leytham</a> scored four tries in succession, a record that still stand today.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The match was played with fifteen players on each side and so was the 1906 match. Played in Wigan again, the match finished a 3–3 draw. The concept was abandoned after the 1906 match. By 1908 the game had expanded much more into Australia, New Zealand and Wales and England began playing those teams. <a href="/wiki/Harold_Wagstaff" title="Harold Wagstaff">Harold Wagstaff</a> made his debut for England in 1908 against the touring Kangaroos team at 17 years and 228 days.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Other Nationalities side did return in 1921.
An England side beat the <a href="/wiki/Australasia" title="Australasia">Australasian</a> team of the <a href="/wiki/1921%E2%80%9322_Kangaroo_tour_of_Great_Britain" title="1921–22 Kangaroo tour of Great Britain">1921–22 Kangaroo tour of Great Britain</a> 4–5 at <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_Stadium" title="Arsenal Stadium">Highbury</a>.  
England played only one international between 10 May 1956 and 7 November 1968 an 18–6 victory at <a href="/wiki/Headingley_Rugby_Stadium" title="Headingley Rugby Stadium">Headingley Rugby Stadium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1975_World_Cup_debut">1975 World Cup debut</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=England_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1975 World Cup debut">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>England played at the <a href="/wiki/1975_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="1975 Rugby League World Cup">World Cup in 1975</a> coached by <a href="/wiki/Alex_Murphy_(rugby_league)" title="Alex Murphy (rugby league)">Alex Murphy</a>, which was played over several months in both hemispheres on a league basis. Normally <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_national_rugby_league_team" title="Great Britain national rugby league team">Great Britain</a> would represent England in the World Cup, but the RLIF wanted to capitalise on the large amount of Welsh players in the game at the time, and so England and Wales fielded separate teams.
</p><p>England won their first match, a 20–2 victory over France in <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a> in March. In June the Lions suffered their first defeat in just their second match of the tournament, losing 12–7 against a strong Wales side in <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a>. A little later England managed to hold on for a draw against Australia in <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a>, the final score being 10–10. And they also picked up a point in <a href="/wiki/Auckland" title="Auckland">Auckland</a>, drawing 17–17 against New Zealand. At the end of October, after the domestic season had finished, England beat the Welsh 22–16 in <a href="/wiki/Warrington" title="Warrington">Warrington</a> and then crossed the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a> to thrash a French side 48–2 in <a href="/wiki/Bordeaux" title="Bordeaux">Bordeaux</a>. Bradford played host the England versus New Zealand match, in which England won comfortably 27–12.
</p><p>At the start of November, England squeezed past Australia winning 16–13 in November at Wigan. This meant that the Kangaroos had finished on 13 points, with the Lions on 12 points. Australia were deemed champions by finishing top of the table, but because they had not beaten England a final match was quickly arranged. Australia beat England 25–0 at Leeds to clinch their fourth title.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1995_World_Cup_and_hiatus">1995 World Cup and hiatus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=England_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1995 World Cup and hiatus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>With the break up of the Great Britain team into its individual nations, England (as co-host) were in the <a href="/wiki/1995_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="1995 Rugby League World Cup">1995 World Cup</a>, their first appearance in the World Cup since 1975. England were coached by <a href="/wiki/Phil_Larder" title="Phil Larder">Phil Larder</a>. The Lions got off to a flying start beating Australia 20–16 in the opening game at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">Wembley</a>, then hammering <a href="/wiki/Fiji_national_rugby_league_team" title="Fiji national rugby league team">Fiji</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Africa_national_rugby_league_team" title="South Africa national rugby league team">South Africa</a> in the remaining group games to finish top of group A. This set up a semi-final game at <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a> against Wales. England won the tussle 25–10 to reach the World Cup final, but they lost 16–8 to Australia at Wembley Stadium. England would not play again until 2000.
</p><p>The 1995 World Cup saw the first change of the England strip in a number of years. Instead of the usual all-white kit, an offset red St George's Cross was added to both the front and back of the jumper.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000_World_Cup">2000 World Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=England_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2000 World Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/John_Kear" title="John Kear">John Kear</a> was coach of England for the <a href="/wiki/2000_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2000 Rugby League World Cup">World Cup in 2000</a>. Compared to 1995, England had little success, losing their opening game at <a href="/wiki/Twickenham_Stadium" title="Twickenham Stadium">Twickenham</a> 22–2 against <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_rugby_league_team" title="Australia national rugby league team">Australia</a>. But they won their remaining two pool games against <a href="/wiki/Fiji_national_rugby_league_team" title="Fiji national rugby league team">Fiji</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russia_national_rugby_league_team" title="Russia national rugby league team">Russia</a>. A surprisingly competitive display by <a href="/wiki/Ireland_national_rugby_league_team" title="Ireland national rugby league team">Ireland</a> in the quarter-finals, saw England scrape through to the semi-finals 26–16. England then went down to a record defeat, losing 49–6 to <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_national_rugby_league_team" title="New Zealand national rugby league team">New Zealand</a> at <a href="/wiki/Bolton" title="Bolton">Bolton</a>, and were knocked out of the tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2008-2009:_Tony_Smith_era">2008-2009: Tony Smith era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=England_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2008-2009: Tony Smith era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a href="/wiki/File:England_2008_RLWC.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/England_2008_RLWC.jpg/400px-England_2008_RLWC.jpg" decoding="async" width="400" height="115" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/England_2008_RLWC.jpg/600px-England_2008_RLWC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/England_2008_RLWC.jpg/800px-England_2008_RLWC.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3180" data-file-height="918" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:England_2008_RLWC.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>England at the <a href="/wiki/2008_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2008 Rugby League World Cup">2008 World Cup</a></div></div></div>
<p>Australian born, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Smith_(rugby_league,_born_1967)" title="Tony Smith (rugby league, born 1967)">Tony Smith</a>, took charge of England in 2008. His first game was against France in Toulouse where the English won 56–8. In his second game, England were missing St Helens and Leeds Rhinos players but the team still created history with a record 74–0 win over Wales in Doncaster. It was England's biggest win recorded over the Welsh since 1978.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> It was <a href="/wiki/2008_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2008 Rugby League World Cup">World Cup year</a>, and Smith announced his ambitions that he wanted England to win their first World Cup, since 1972, when Great Britain represented the country at the event. In the event they were placed in Group A alongside hosts Australia, New Zealand and Papua New Guinea. England faced a scare in their opening game against Papua New Guinea, as Smith's men were trailing 12–16 at halftime, but they did go on to win the game. England were humiliated in their second game against the hosts, suffering their biggest defeat to date, beating their 43-point margin against New Zealand eight years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> In their final pool game against New Zealand, they produced a much better performance but for only 28 minutes, as they gave up a 24–8 lead to lose 24–36. Before, and during the match, England were accusing New Zealand of being soft, however, after the match, media outlets were calling England the biggest losers of the tournament. Controversy also occurred before the game kicked off, when England refused to face New Zealand's haka challenge. Smith said 'In some cultures poking your tongue out at others could be seen as insulting and the Kiwis pushed things too far by crossing into England’s side of halfway.'<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> They took on New Zealand again in the semi-final. This time they never had the lead over the Kiwis, as they lost the match by 10 points. After rumours Smith would be sacked from his position, the RFL announced they'd keep faith in Smith for the remainder of his contract. The World Cup players took the blame for their performances.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the World Cup nightmare, England began 2009 on a high-note with a record breaking 54 point away win over France.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Later that year, England were co-hosts of the year's major international tournament, the inaugural <a href="/wiki/2009_Four_Nations" class="mw-redirect" title="2009 Four Nations">Four Nations</a>. After thrashing them earlier in the year, England faced a shock half-time deficit in their opening game against a French side coached by former Great Britain international <a href="/wiki/Bobbie_Goulding" title="Bobbie Goulding">Bobbie Goulding</a>. But despite trailing at the interval, England scored 30 consecutive points to record another victory over 'Les Tricolores'. In the second match against Australia, England impressively kept Australia scoreless in the second-half, and staged a second-half comeback. However it wasn't enough, as Smith's men needed to recover from a 26-point half-time deficit. They then took on New Zealand and, after losing to them twice at last year's World Cup, England earned revenge with an 8-point win over the Kiwis. England then went on to make the final to face Australia. In the final England, at one point, led 16–14 and were credited with how they were able to produce a real contest. However, in the final quarter of the game, Australia dominated proceedings and eventually went on to win 46–16. On 16 November 2009, a few hours after crediting that the England national team had a bright future in rugby league, Smith resigned from the English national side.
</p>
<h3><span id="2010.E2.80.932015:_Steve_McNamara_era"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2010–2015:_Steve_McNamara_era">2010–2015: Steve McNamara era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=England_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2010–2015: Steve McNamara era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following Tony Smiths resignation, former <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Bulls" title="Bradford Bulls">Bradford Bulls</a> head coach <a href="/wiki/Steve_McNamara" title="Steve McNamara">Steve McNamara</a> was given the job. His first game in charge of England was against France in Leigh. England thrashed the French to keep their impressive winning run going over their opponents that dates back to 1981. McNamara also fielded the first brothers, <a href="/wiki/Sam_Tomkins" title="Sam Tomkins">Sam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joel_Tomkins" title="Joel Tomkins">Joel Tomkins</a>, to start on the field for England since <a href="/wiki/Paul_Hulme" title="Paul Hulme">Paul</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Hulme_(rugby_league)" title="David Hulme (rugby league)">David Hulme</a> represented Great Britain in 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The following year, England co-hosted the <a href="/wiki/2011_Rugby_League_Four_Nations" title="2011 Rugby League Four Nations">2011 Four Nations</a> with Wales. Their opening game was a win against Wales where Sam Tomkins scored a record-equalling four tries in one game. The win meant England kept their impressive record of not losing on home soil against Wales since 1977. A loss the following week to Australia at Wembley meant that they had to beat New Zealand to make the final, which they did. In the final, England at one point were tied at 8–8, but they would be outclassed again. England were held 'try-less' in the second half as Australia won by 22 points.
</p><p>In mid-2012, the second <a href="/wiki/2012_International_Origin_series" title="2012 International Origin series">International Origin series</a> was held. The Exiles had won the first series in 2011 after Samoan International, George Carmont, scored a try with less than 40 seconds remaining to win the game for the Exiles. England won their first ever International Origin series game, after winning game 1 of the 2012 series, held in St Helens, by 8 points. However the Exiles would win the 2012 series after recording a bigger winning margin in game 2. In October and November that year, England competed in the <a href="/wiki/2012_Autumn_International_Series" title="2012 Autumn International Series">Autumn Internationals</a> where they took on Wales, and France. In their first game, England racked up their biggest points tally against Wales, as they thrashed 'the Red Dragons' 80–12 in Wrexham.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> In their second game against France, fullback Sam Tomkins became England's top try scorer when he scored his 14th try for England, breaking the record set by former Wigan and St Helens winger <a href="/wiki/Alf_Ellaby" title="Alf Ellaby">Alf Ellaby</a> in 1935.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> In the final, England had a rematch with France at Salford City Stadium. England thrashed their opponents to win their first tournament title since the 2004 European Nations Cup.
</p><p>In the lone <a href="/wiki/2013_International_Origin_series" title="2013 International Origin series">2013 International Origin</a> game, England thrashed their opponents by 20 points. At the end of the year, the <a href="/wiki/2013_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2013 Rugby League World Cup">2013 World Cup</a> was held in England and Wales. England, who were now known as the 'Wall of White', featured a new record of three brothers in their squad: <a href="/wiki/Sam_Burgess" title="Sam Burgess">Sam</a> and twins <a href="/wiki/George_Burgess_(rugby_league)" title="George Burgess (rugby league)">George</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tom_Burgess_(rugby_league)" title="Tom Burgess (rugby league)">Tom Burgess</a>. England played their first game against Australia in Cardiff. England got off to a surprising early lead for many, when they were up 10–0 after 20 minutes. England, however, went on to lose in what was one of their best displays against the Kangaroos in years, losing 20–28. They then went on to thrash Ireland to nil in front of a record crowd in Huddersfield, in a game which saw <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Hall_(rugby_league)" title="Ryan Hall (rugby league)">Ryan Hall</a> become the new England top try-scorer after a hat-trick took him to tally 17 total tries for his country. England also beat a determined Fiji, in front a sold-out crowd at the KC Stadium, to advance to the quarter-finals. They took on European rivals, France, in Wigan and, after trailing 0–6 early, England went on to advance to the semi-finals to meet defending World Champions, New Zealand, at Wembley. The game was a see-saw affair, which saw England leading 18–14 with one minute on the clock remaining, until New Zealand play-maker Shaun Johnson produced a historical moment, to level the scores, and then convert his try after the siren, to win the match, and make the Kiwis advance to a third consecutive World Cup Final. This was the first time England, or Great Britain, had lost to New Zealand in England since 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October and November 2014, England travelled down-under to play in the <a href="/wiki/2014_Rugby_League_Four_Nations" title="2014 Rugby League Four Nations">2014 Four Nations</a>. In the opening game, England took on Samoa in an affair which saw the lead change several times. In the end, England survived a shock result occurring after winning by 6 points. In the second game against Australia, controversy occurred. Australia led 16–12 with one minute left on the clock. England player, <a href="/wiki/Liam_Farrell" title="Liam Farrell">Liam Farrell</a>, put a grubber-kick in the in-goal area, which forced Australian fullback, Greg Inglis, to force the ball dead, however, the video referees decided to have a look and see whether or not Inglis or the incoming Ryan Hall got the last touch on the ball. On the slow-motion replays, it showed that Ryan Hall's right hand's little finger had put some downward pressure on the ball, however, in normal speed, it was deemed 'inconclusive' by Australian officiating rules. It was eventually given a no-try to the anger of English players and fans. Ryan complained on Twitter, saying "Looking at the video, I’d say it was a try if we’re playing Super League rules..." Had Hall scored, and England converted, it would have been England's first win over Australia since 1995, the first time Australia suffered back-to-back home defeats since 1970 and the first time Australia did not qualify for a tournament final since the 1954 World Cup final.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> England lost their final game against New Zealand and, in the process, ended any chance of qualifying for their first Four Nations final in the Southern Hemisphere.
</p><p>In 2015, England took on New Zealand in a <a href="/wiki/2015_New_Zealand_rugby_league_tour_of_Great_Britain" class="mw-redirect" title="2015 New Zealand rugby league tour of Great Britain">three match series</a> held in England. Before the series, England recorded their biggest ever win over France, beating their previous 73–6 win in 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> England beat New Zealand 2–1 in the Baskerville Series to retain the trophy that Great Britain last won in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> During that series vice-captain, <a href="/wiki/James_Graham_(rugby_league)" title="James Graham (rugby league)">James Graham</a>, reached the milestone of becoming England's most capped player, surpassing <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Sinfield" title="Kevin Sinfield">Kevin Sinfield</a>'s record of 27 test appearances.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Despite the series victory, McNamara was facing scrutiny beforehand and the RFL decided not to renew his contract which expired after the series. McNamara therefore left the England national team.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2016-present:_Wayne_Bennett_era">2016-present: Wayne Bennett era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=England_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2016-present: Wayne Bennett era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following McNamara's contract expiration, the RFL appointed Australian <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Bennett_(rugby_league)" title="Wayne Bennett (rugby league)">Wayne Bennett</a> on a 2-year contract, with a view to win the 2017 World Cup. Bennett's first request as coach was for England to have a pre-season training camp, a mid-season international in 2017, as well as shortening the 2017 Super League season in order to prepare for the <a href="/wiki/2017_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2017 Rugby League World Cup">2017 World Cup</a>. RFL Chief Executive Nigel Wood accepted Bennett's first two demands, but said shortening the domestic season is a "big disturbance in lots of ways..."<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Bennett's plans suffered criticism from some professional club coaches.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> 
Bennett's first <a href="/wiki/2016_Rugby_League_Four_Nations#France_vs_England" title="2016 Rugby League Four Nations">match</a> was against France in Perpignan, in preparation for the <a href="/wiki/2016_Rugby_League_Four_Nations" title="2016 Rugby League Four Nations">2016 Four Nations</a>. Despite trailing, and being held scoreless in the first 26 minutes, England did go on to avoid an upset, convincingly beating the French and giving Bennett a successful return to the International scene, 8 years after he left the New Zealand assistant coach role. However England went onto having a disappointing Four Nations, losing the opening game to New Zealand, facing a scare against Scotland, before going on to lose a 'must-win' game against Australia. This marked the first time that England failed to qualify for a Four Nations final while being hosts.
</p><p>At the end of 2016, Bennett announced that the England pre-season 'heat training camp' in Dubai would be cancelled after taking in the consideration of domestic coaches' concerns.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Instead of a pre-season training camp, Bennett and the English coaching staff chose an Elite Performance Squad of players, based in England, who would be scouted regularly throughout the 2017 season. The squad trained six times throughout the season in England.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>England's first game of 2017 was a convincing result over Samoa, although Bennett came under criticism of his selections for the <a href="/wiki/2017_Pacific_Rugby_League_Tests#England_vs_Samoa" title="2017 Pacific Rugby League Tests">test-match</a>. Former Great Britain captain <a href="/wiki/Garry_Schofield" title="Garry Schofield">Garry Schofield</a>, along with other former players, media, and fans were angered by Bennett's decision to include Australian born players <a href="/wiki/Chris_McQueen" title="Chris McQueen">Chris McQueen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Heighington" title="Chris Heighington">Chris Heighington</a>, who are eligible to play through their English fathers. Heighington's age was also a talking point. At the age of 35, it was suggested younger players such as <a href="/wiki/Liam_Farrell" title="Liam Farrell">Liam Farrell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alex_Walmsley" title="Alex Walmsley">Alex Walmsley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Percival" title="Mark Percival">Mark Percival</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Scott_Taylor_(rugby_league)" title="Scott Taylor (rugby league)">Scott Taylor</a>, should have been selected instead.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Bennett only named one Australian, Chris Heighnington, in his England team for the World Cup, while <a href="/wiki/Zak_Hardaker" title="Zak Hardaker">Zak Hardaker</a> missed out due to a drugs ban. England's first game of the World Cup was against Australia. Although they were credited throughout the match for the way they were able to defend and prevent the Australians from dominating the game like they have in the past they again failed to beat Australia. Despite the defeat, England continued their way through the tournament with convincing victories over Lebanon, France, finishing second in Group A. They then went on to beat Papua New Guinea convincingly in the quarter finals before reaching the semi-finals where they would take on Tonga who had knocked New Zealand out the week before. England led 20–0, with seven minutes left on the clock, before the Tongans began an unpredictable and nerve-wracking comeback for England. With less than one minute left on the clock, Andrew Fifita lost control of the ball before regathering it and putting it over the try-line, only to realise the referee had already blown his whistle. The referee was criticised for not going to the Video Referee and if awarded would have seen that Tonga won the game and reached their first ever World Cup final.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Despite the controversy, England were victorious and had advanced to their first World Cup Final in 22 Years.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> England met Australia again in the <a href="/wiki/2017_Rugby_League_World_Cup_Final" title="2017 Rugby League World Cup Final">final</a> but again failed to beat Australia, for a 13th consecutive time, since their last win in the 1995 World Cup group stage. England lost in the lowest World Cup final score in the history of the tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Bennets contract expired at the end of the World Cup and despite not winning the tournament he was rewarded with another 2-year contract.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Identity">Identity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=England_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Identity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kits_and_colours">Kits and colours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=England_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Kits and colours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>England traditionally play in white while they occasionally play in a red away kit but colour clashes are rare and they rarely wear an away kit.
</p><p>While there original strip was white with red hoops, in the 1975 World Cup they played in a fully white kit. It wasn't until 1995 when they began wearing their iconic cross on the front of their kit.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kit_evolution">Kit evolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=England_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Kit evolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Badge">Badge</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=England_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Badge">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><b>The Lions crest</b></li></ul>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_England_RL_Logo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/aa/Old_England_RL_Logo.jpg/100px-Old_England_RL_Logo.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/aa/Old_England_RL_Logo.jpg/150px-Old_England_RL_Logo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/aa/Old_England_RL_Logo.jpg/200px-Old_England_RL_Logo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="264" data-file-height="377" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_England_RL_Logo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The old logo was used from the mid 1990s until 2008</div></div></div>
<p>From the 1995 Rugby League World cup, it was used a crest with the <a href="/wiki/St._George%27s_cross" class="mw-redirect" title="St. George&#39;s cross">St. George's cross</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Coat of arms of England">Three Lions Coat of Arms of England</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tudor_rose" title="Tudor rose">Tudor rose</a>. It was similar to most other English sporting badges, such as the <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England national football team</a> and the <a href="/wiki/English_national_cricket_team" class="mw-redirect" title="English national cricket team">English national cricket team</a> which all promote similar attributes. Until the mid 1990s, England simply used a red <a href="/wiki/Rampant_lion" class="mw-redirect" title="Rampant lion">Rampant lion</a> as crest.
</p>
<ul><li><b>The Shield Crest</b></li></ul>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EnglandRugbyLeagueLions.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/21/EnglandRugbyLeagueLions.png/100px-EnglandRugbyLeagueLions.png" decoding="async" width="100" height="117" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/21/EnglandRugbyLeagueLions.png/150px-EnglandRugbyLeagueLions.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/21/EnglandRugbyLeagueLions.png/200px-EnglandRugbyLeagueLions.png 2x" data-file-width="257" data-file-height="300" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EnglandRugbyLeagueLions.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The last logo was used until 2017</div></div></div>
<p>The new official logo was launched on 6 February 2008 on the rugby league magazine programme <a href="/wiki/Boots_N%27_All" class="mw-redirect" title="Boots N&#39; All">Boots N' All</a>. The cross of St George is positioned across a three-dimensional shield within the design. The date "1895" is placed through the centre of the cross, symbolising the birth of rugby league. Many people involved in the sport were consulted throughout the design process, which took a little under a year. The logo was first used for the <a href="/wiki/2008_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2008 Rugby League World Cup">2008 World Cup</a> and was replaced in 2017.
</p>
<ul><li><b>Three Lions Cross</b></li></ul>
<p>As part of a rebrand across all of the RFL in 2017, a new England crest was introduced. It is a merge of both the shield crest and the old lions crest. It has the St. Georges cross on the background with three lions in front of it.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_coverage">Media coverage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=England_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Media coverage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> have the rights to screen all England games. They showed every game England competed in at the <a href="/wiki/2017_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2017 Rugby League World Cup">2017 Rugby League World Cup</a>, as well as all their <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_Four_Nations" title="Rugby League Four Nations">Four Nations</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Baskerville_Shield" title="Baskerville Shield">Baskerville Shield</a> games.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Team_Records">Team Records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=England_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Team Records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>Biggest win:</li></ul>
<dl><dd><dl><dd>110-0 <i>v.</i> <span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1235" data-file-height="650" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/United_States_national_rugby_league_team" title="United States national rugby league team">United States</a> (at <a href="/wiki/Orlando" class="mw-redirect" title="Orlando">Orlando</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>, October 2000)</dd></dl></dd></dl>
<ul><li>Biggest loss:</li></ul>
<dl><dd><dl><dd>52-4 <i>v.</i> <span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg/46px-Flag_of_Australia_%28converted%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="640" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Australia_national_rugby_league_team" title="Australia national rugby league team">Australia</a> (at <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Rectangular_Stadium" title="Melbourne Rectangular Stadium">Melbourne Rectangular Stadium</a>, 2 November 2008)</dd></dl></dd></dl>
<ul><li>Highest all-time attendance:</li></ul>
<dl><dd><dl><dd>67,545 <i>v.</i> <span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Flag_of_New_Zealand.svg/23px-Flag_of_New_Zealand.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Flag_of_New_Zealand.svg/35px-Flag_of_New_Zealand.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Flag_of_New_Zealand.svg/46px-Flag_of_New_Zealand.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_national_rugby_league_team" title="New Zealand national rugby league team">New Zealand</a> (at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley</a>, 23 November 2013)</dd></dl></dd></dl>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Competitive_record">Competitive record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=England_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Competitive record">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/England_national_rugby_league_team_match_results" class="mw-redirect" title="England national rugby league team match results">England national rugby league team match results</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overall_record">Overall record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=England_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Overall record">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>England have played 206 competitive (non friendly or exhibition) games in their history, with the first being played in 1904.  The team have only been playing regularly since 1995, playing 91 of their games from then up to and including the third test of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=2018_Baskerville_Shield&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="2018 Baskerville Shield (page does not exist)">2018 Baskerville Shield</a> against <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_national_rugby_league_team" title="New Zealand national rugby league team">New Zealand</a>.  This means that in the preceding 91 years before 1995, the team played just 116 games.  The reason for this lack of games is because the home nations were represented by <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_national_rugby_league_team" title="Great Britain national rugby league team">Great Britain</a> for most of the 20th century, playing 322 games.  England and the other home nations mainly only played in the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_European_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Rugby League European Cup">European Cup</a> while England and <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_rugby_league_team" title="Wales national rugby league team">Wales</a> regularly played friendlies in the earlier decades of the 20th century. If games played by the Great Britain team are taken into account, English players have actually taken part in 529 games between 1904 and 2018 up to and including the third Baskerville Shield test of 2018.
</p><p>England have played 21 different teams over their history with 6 of these being representative teams.  They hold a 0% win record against only one national team, <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_rugby_league_team" title="Italy national rugby league team">Italy</a>, by whom they were beaten 14-15 in a friendly at the <a href="/wiki/AJ_Bell_Stadium" title="AJ Bell Stadium">AJ Bell Stadium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salford,_Greater_Manchester" class="mw-redirect" title="Salford, Greater Manchester">Salford</a> as a warm-up to the <a href="/wiki/2013_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2013 Rugby League World Cup">2013 World Cup</a>.  England have played <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_rugby_league_team" title="Wales national rugby league team">Wales</a> the most, with 69 games played, winning 50 of these. Because the home nations were represented by Great Britain for most of their history England have only played <a href="/wiki/Ireland_national_rugby_league_team" title="Ireland national rugby league team">Ireland</a> 3 times and <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_rugby_league_team" title="Scotland national rugby league team">Scotland</a> once.
</p><p>England played their 206th game when they took on New Zealand in the third 2018 test at <a href="/wiki/Elland_Road" title="Elland Road">Elland Road</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leeds,_West_Yorkshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Leeds, West Yorkshire">Leeds</a>.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Cup">World Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=England_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: World Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="Rugby League World Cup">Rugby League World Cup</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/England_at_the_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="England at the Rugby League World Cup">England at the Rugby League World Cup</a></div>
<p>England have competed six times in the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="Rugby League World Cup">World Cup</a>; in <a href="/wiki/1975_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="1975 Rugby League World Cup">1975</a>, <a href="/wiki/1995_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="1995 Rugby League World Cup">1995</a>, <a href="/wiki/2000_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2000 Rugby League World Cup">2000</a>, <a href="/wiki/2008_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2008 Rugby League World Cup">2008</a>, <a href="/wiki/2013_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2013 Rugby League World Cup">2013</a> and <a href="/wiki/2017_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2017 Rugby League World Cup">2017</a>. They have never won the competition, though finished runners-up to Australia in 1975, 1995 and 2017. In every other year, <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_national_rugby_league_team" title="Great Britain national rugby league team">Great Britain</a> have represented England. Despite having only played in 6 world cups, England have hosted matches in 8 different tournaments including 3 that took part internationally. England have played 34 games in the world cup; winning 20, drawing 2 and losing 12. Of those losses, only one has been against a team other than <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_national_rugby_league_team" title="New Zealand national rugby league team">New Zealand</a> or <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_rugby_league_team" title="Australia national rugby league team">Australia</a>, when <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_rugby_league_team" title="Wales national rugby league team">Wales</a> won 7-12 in the 1975 tournament. England lost out on reaching the final in 2013, when <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_national_rugby_league_team" title="New Zealand national rugby league team">New Zealand</a> beat them 20-18 after <a href="/wiki/Shaun_Johnson" title="Shaun Johnson">Shaun Johnson</a> scored a conversion in the last 30 seconds of the game to secure the win.  England reached the world cup final in 2017, but were beaten by Australia with a score of just 6-0.
</p><p>As hosts of the <a href="/wiki/2021_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2021 Rugby League World Cup">2021 Rugby League World Cup</a> and as a team who reached the quarter finals in the previous world cup, England automatically qualified.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Four_Nations">Four Nations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=England_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Four Nations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_Four_Nations" title="Rugby League Four Nations">Rugby League Four Nations</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/England_at_the_Four_Nations" title="England at the Four Nations">England at the Four Nations</a></div>
<p>England replaced Great Britain in competing in the Rugby League Four Nations which replaced the previous Tri Nations tournament. They have been runners up twice in 2009 and 2011, these two tournaments also having been hosted by England.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Championship">European Championship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=England_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: European Championship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_European_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Rugby League European Cup">Rugby League European Cup</a></div>
<p>England have competed in twenty-six European Nations Cups, the first in 1935. In the past the tournament has been axed and revived many times, and it was stopped for six years because of the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>. From 1935 to 1949 (minus the war years) England played France and Wales annually, and won the tournament in 1935, 1946, 1947 and 1948. From 1950 to 1956 an Other Nationalities team were added as the fourth team in the competition (except in 1956 when Wales did not field a team). During those years England won in 1950 and 1954. Since then the tournament has run for some seasons, but never for more than five years at a time. But from 1970 to 1996 England won it six out of a possible nine times. In 2003 the tournament was revived and England comfortably won, beating her old rivals plus Scotland, Ireland and Russia. England beat the same opponents to win the cup again in 2004. This was the last time England competed to give the competition more of a level playing field for other teams, however the <a href="/wiki/England_Knights" title="England Knights">England Knights</a> competed in 2012.
</p>

<p><i>Major:</i><br />
<b><a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="Rugby League World Cup">World Cup</a></b>: 
<br /><b>Runners-up</b> (3): 1975, 1995, 2017
<br /><b>Semi-finalists</b> (3): 2000, 2008, 2013
</p><p><b><a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_Four_Nations" title="Rugby League Four Nations">Four Nations</a></b>:
<br /><b>Runners-up</b> (2): 2009, 2011
</p><p><i>Regional:</i><br />
<b><a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_European_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Rugby League European Cup">European Championship</a></b>: 
<br /><b>Winners</b> (14):1935, 1945–46, 1946–47, 1947–48, 1949–50, 1953–54, 1969–70, 1975, 1978, 1979, 1980, 1996, 2003, 2004
</p><p><i>Minor:</i><br />
<b><a href="/wiki/Federation_Shield" title="Federation Shield">Federation Shield</a></b>:
<br /><b>Winners</b> (1): 2006
</p><p><b><a href="/wiki/Baskerville_Shield" title="Baskerville Shield">Baskerville Shield</a></b>:
<br /><b>Winners</b> (1): 2015, 2018

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_England_teams">Other England teams</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=England_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Other England teams">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="England_Knights">England Knights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=England_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: England Knights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/England_Knights" title="England Knights">England Knights</a></div>
<p>In 2011 the <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England Knights</a> were created to serve as a step up for the younger players from their club in view of playing for the 1st team. A squad of players were chosen (below the age of 25) to represent the Knights in a few games. Their first ever game was against France and the Knights came out 38–18 victors.
</p><p>The Knights won the <a href="/wiki/2012_European_Cup_(rugby_league)" title="2012 European Cup (rugby league)">2012 European Cup</a> by beating <a href="/wiki/Ireland_national_rugby_league_team" title="Ireland national rugby league team">Ireland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_rugby_league_team" title="Scotland national rugby league team">Scotland</a> in a 3-game tournament.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="England_Lionesses">England Lionesses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=England_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: England Lionesses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/England_Lionesses" class="mw-redirect" title="England Lionesses">England Lionesses</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Famous_players">Famous players</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=England_national_rugby_league_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Famous players">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The following players played for England and are either <a href="/wiki/British_Rugby_League_Hall_of_Fame" class="mw-redirect" title="British Rugby League Hall of Fame">British Rugby League Hall of Fame</a> inductees, or are one of the top five caps, tries, goals, or points scorers for England. Although both <a href="/wiki/Gus_Risman" title="Gus Risman">Gus Risman</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jim_Sullivan_(rugby_league)" title="Jim Sullivan (rugby league)">Jim Sullivan</a> were <a href="/wiki/Welsh_people" title="Welsh people">Welsh</a>, they are British Rugby League Hall of Fame inductees, and actually played for England, as well as for <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_rugby_league_team" title="Wales national rugby league team">Wales</a> and <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_national_rugby_league_team" title="Great Britain national rugby league team">Great Britain</a>. British Rugby League Hall of Fame inductee <a href="/wiki/Vince_Karalius" title="Vince Karalius">Vince Karalius</a> was English (of <a href="/wiki/Lithuanian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Lithuanian people">Lithuanian</a> heritage), and although he played for Great Britain, he never played for England, as England games were limited in his playing era.
</p>
